<h2>26</h2>
<p>Annex II</p>
<p>referred to in Article 10</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1</p>
<p>Export aid prohibited by this Agreement</p>
<p>(a) Currency retention schemes or any similar practices which involve a<br>bonus on exports or re-exports.</p>
<p>(b) The provision by governments of direct subsidies to exporters.</p>
<p>(c) The remission, calculated in relation to exports, of direct taxes or social<br>welfare charges on industrial or commercial enterprises.</p>
<p>(d) The exemption, in respect of exported goods, from charges or taxes,<br>other than charges in connection with importation or indirect taxes<br>levied at one or several stages on the same goods if sold for internal<br>consumption, or the payment, in respect of exported goods, of amounts<br>exceeding those effectively levied at one or several stages on these goods<br>in the form of indirect taxes or of charges in connection with importation<br>or in both forms.</p>
<p>(e) In respect of deliveries by governments or governmental agencies of<br>imported raw materials for export business on different terms than for<br>domestic business, the charging of prices below world prices.</p>
<p>(f) In respect of government export credit guarantees, the charging of<br>premiums at rates which are manifestly inadequate to cover the long-<br>term operating costs and losses of the credit insurance institutions.</p>
<p>(g) The grant by governments (or special institutions controlled by govern-<br>ments) of export credits at rates below those which they have to pay in<br>order to obtain the funds so employed.</p>
<p>(h) The government bearing all or part of the costs incurred by exporters in<br>obtaining credit.</p>
<p>27</p>
<p>Bilaga II</p>
<p>som avses i artikel 10</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1</p>
<p>Exportstöd som är förbjudet enligt detta avtal</p>
<p>a) &nbsp;System, varigenom exportör får förfoga över del av intjänad valuta, eller<br>liknande förfarande innebärande premiering av export eller reexport.</p>
<p>b) &nbsp;Direkta statliga subventioner till exportörer.</p>
<p>c) &nbsp;Åtgärder, varigenom industri- eller handelsföretag befrias från direkta<br>skatter eller sociala avgifter i förhållande till verkställd export.</p>
<p>d) &nbsp;Åtgärder, varigenom vid export av varor andra avgifter eller skatter ef-<br>terskänks än sådana avgifter, som utgår i samband med import, eller så-<br>dana indirekta skatter, som i ett eller flera led erläggs för samma slags<br>varor vid försäljning för inhemsk förbrukning, eller åtgärder, varigenom<br>vid export av varor belopp utbetalas, som överstiger vad som i verklighe-<br>ten i ett eller flera led uttagits för dessa varor i form av indirekta skatter<br>och/eller avgifter i samband med import.</p>
<p>e) &nbsp;Debitering av lägre priser än världsmarknadspriserna i fall då statliga<br>myndigheter eller organ vid sina leveranser av importerade råvaror till-<br>lämpar olika villkor beroende på om leveranserna avser exportändamål<br>eller inhemsk förbrukning.</p>
<p>f) &nbsp;Tillämpning av sådana premiesatser vid statlig exportkreditgarantigiv-<br>ning, som är uppenbart otillräckliga för att täcka kreditförsäkringsinsti-<br>tutens kostnader och förluster på längre sikt.</p>
<p>g) &nbsp;Beviljande genom statliga myndigheter (eller särskilda institutioner un-<br>der statlig kontroll) av exportkrediter till lägre ränta än myndigheterna<br>(eller institutionerna) själva får erlägga för att anskaffa motsvarande ka-<br>pital.</p>
<p>h) &nbsp;Åtgärder innebärande att staten helt eller delvis svarar för kostnader,<br>som exportörer ådrar sig i samband med anskaffande av krediter.</p>
<p>28</p>
<p>ProtocolA</p>
<p>Concerning the Definition of the Concept of<br>“Originating Products” and Methods of<br>Administrative Cooperation</p>
<p>Title I</p>
<p>Definition of the concept of “originating products”</p>
<p>Article 1</p>
<p>1. For the purpose of implementing the Agreement, and without prejudice<br>to the provisions of Article 2, the following products shall be considered as<br>products originating in Latvia or in Sweden.</p>
<p>(a) products wholly obtained in Latvia or in Sweden within the mea-<br>ning of Article 4;</p>
<p>(b) products obtained in Latvia or in Sweden incorporating materials<br>which have not been wholly obtained there, provided that:</p>
<p>(i) &nbsp;such materials have undergone sufficient working or Proces-<br>sing in Latvia or in Sweden within the meaning of Article 5, or<br>that</p>
<p>(ii) such materials originate in the other Party to this Agreement,<br>within the meaning of this Protocol, or that</p>
<p>(iii) such materials originate in Estonia or in Lithuania in applica-<br>tion of the origin rules in the Agreements establishing Free<br>Trade Areas between Sweden on the one side and Estonia or<br>Lithuania on the other, in so far as the said rules are identical<br>to those of this Protocol.</p>
<p>2. For products obtained in Latvia the provisions of paragraph 1 (b) (iii) may<br>be applied only on condition that the necessary administrative co-operation<br>between Latvia, Estonia and Lithuania for the implementation of these pro-<br>visions has been established in accordance with the provisions of this Proto-<br>col.</p>
<p>Article 2</p>
<p>1. Notwithstanding the provisions of sub-paragraphs (b) (ii) and (iii) of pa-<br>ragraph 1 of Article 1, products originating within the meaning of this Proto-<br>col in Latvia or in Sweden or in Estonia or Lithuania in application of the<br>origin rules referred to in sub-paragraph (b) (iii) of paragraph 1 of Article 1,<br>and exported from one State Party to this Agreement to the other in the same<br>State or having undergone in the exporting State no working or processing<br>going beyond that referred to in paragraph 5 of Article 5, retain their origin.</p>
<p>2. For the purpose of implementing paragraph 1, where products originating<br>in Latvia and in Sweden or in one or both of these States and Estonia and/or<br>Lithuania are used and those products have undergone no working or pro-<br>cessing in the exporting State going beyond that referred to in paragraph 5<br>of Article 5, the origin is determined by the product with the highest customs</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>29</p>
<p>value or, if this is not known and cannot be ascertained, with the highest first Prop. 1991/92:142<br>ascertainable price paid for the products in that State. &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>Article 3</p>
<p>(This protocol does not contain an Article 3)</p>
<p>Article 4</p>
<p>The following shall be considered as wholly obtained in Latvia or in Sweden<br>within the meaning of sub-paragraph (a) of paragraph 1 of Article 1:</p>
<p>(a) mineral products extracted from its soil or from its seabed;</p>
<p>(b) vegetable products harvested there;</p>
<p>(c) live animals born and raised there;</p>
<p>(d) products from live animals raised there;</p>
<p>(e) products obtained by hunting or fishing conducted there;</p>
<p>(f) products of sea fishing and other products taken from the sea by its<br>vessels;</p>
<p>(g) products made aboard its factory ships exclusively from products<br>referred to in subparagraph (f);</p>
<p>(h) used artides collected there fit only for the recovery of raw mate-<br>rials, subject to Note 5a on used tyres contained in Annex I to this<br>Protocol;</p>
<p>(i) waste and scrap resulting from manufacturing operations conducted<br>there;</p>
<p>(j) goods produced there exclusively from products specified in sub-pa-<br>ragraphs (a) to (i).</p>
<p>Article 5</p>
<p>1. The expressions “Chapters” and “headings” used in this Protocol shall<br>mean the Chapters and the headings (four digit codes) used in the Nomencla-<br>ture which makes up the “Harmonized Commodity Description and Coding<br>System” (hereinafter referred to as the Harmonized System or HS). The ex-<br>pression “classified” shall refer to the classification of a product or material<br>under a particular heading.</p>
<p>2. For the purposes of Article 1, non-originating materials are considered to<br>be sufficiently worked or processed when the products obtained is classified<br>within a heading which is different from those in which all the non-origina-<br>ting materials used in its manufacture are classified, subject to the provisions<br>of paragraphs 3, 4 and 5.</p>
<p>3. For a product mentioned in columns 1 and 2 of the List in Annex II to this<br>Protocol, the conditions set out in column 3 for the product concerned must<br>be fulfilled instead of the rule in paragraph 2.</p>
<p>4. For the products of Chapters 84 to 91 inclusive, as an alternative to satis-<br>fying the conditions set out in column 3, the exporter may opt to apply the<br>conditions set out in column 4 instead.</p>
<p>30</p>
<p>5. For the purpose of implementing sub-paragraph (b) (i) of paragraph 1 of<br>Article 1 the following shall still be considered as insufficient working or Pro-<br>cessing to confer the status of originating product, whether or not there is a<br>change of heading:</p>
<p>(a) operations to ensure the preservation of merchandise in good con-<br>dition during transport and storage (ventilation, spreading out,<br>drying, chilling, placing in salt, sulphur dioxide or other aqueous<br>Solutions, removal damaged parts, and like operations);</p>
<p>(b) simple operations consisting of removal of dust, sifting or scree-<br>ning, sorting, classifying, matching (including the making-up of sets<br>of artides), washing, painting, cutting up;</p>
<p>(c) (i) changes of packing and breaking up and assembly of consign-<br>ments;</p>
<p>(ii) simple placing in bottles, fläsks, bags, cases, boxes, fixing on<br>cards or boards, etc., and all other simple packing operations;</p>
<p>(d) affixing marks, labels or other like distinguishing signs on products<br>or their packaging;</p>
<p>(e) simple mixing of products, whether or not of different kinds, where<br>one or more components of the mixtures do not meet the conditions<br>laid down in this Protocol to enable them to be considered as origi-<br>nating products;</p>
<p>(f) simple assembly of parts of artides to constitute a complete article;</p>
<p>(g) a combination of two or more operations specified in subpara-<br>graphs (a) to (f);</p>
<p>(h) slaughter of animals.</p>
<p>Article 6</p>
<p>1. The term “value” in the List in Annex II shall mean the customs value at<br>the time of the import of the non-originating materials used or, if this is not<br>known and cannot be ascertained, the first ascertainable price paid for the<br>materials in the territory concerned.</p>
<p>Where the value of the originating materials used needs to be established,<br>this paragraph shall be applied mutatis mutandis.</p>
<p>2. The term “ex-works price” in the List in Annex II shall mean the ex-works<br>price of the product obtained minus any internal taxes which are, or may be,<br>repaid when the product obtained is exported.</p>
<p>Article 7</p>
<p>Goods originating in the sense of this Protocol and constituting a single ship-<br>ment which is not split up may be transported through territory other than<br>that of Latvia, Sweden, Estonia or Lithuania with, should the occasion arise,<br>transshipment or temporary warehousing in such territory, provided that the<br>Crossing of latter territory is justified for geographical reasons, that the goods<br>have remained under the surveillance of the customs authorities in the<br>country of transit or of warehousing, that they have not entered into the<br>commerce of such countries or been delivered for home use there and have</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>31</p>
<p>not undergone operations other than unloading, reloading or any operation Prop. 1991/92:142<br>designed to preserve them in good condition. &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>Title II</p>
<p>Methods for administrative cooperation</p>
<p>Article 8</p>
<p>1. Originating products whithin the meaning of this Protocol shall, on im-<br>portation into Latvia or Sweden, benefit from the Agreement upon submis-<br>sion of one of the following documents:</p>
<p>(a) an EUR.l movement certificate, hereinafter referred to as an<br>“EUR.l certificate” or an EUR.l certificate, valid for a long term,<br>and invoices referring to such certificate made out in accordance<br>with Article 13. Aspecimenof the EUR.l certificate is given in An-<br>nex III to this Protocol;</p>
<p>(b) an invoice bearing the exporter’s declaration as given in Annex IV<br>to this Protocol, made out in accordance with Article 13;</p>
<p>(c) an invoice bearing the exporter’s declaration as given in Annex IV<br>to this Protocol, made out by any exporter for any consignment con-<br>sisting of one or more packages containing originating products<br>whose total value does not exceed 5,110 units of account.</p>
<p>2. The following originating products within the meaning of this Protocol<br>shall, on importation into Latvia or Sweden, benefit from the Agreement<br>without it being necessary to produce any of the documents referred to in<br>paragraph 1:</p>
<p>(a) products sent as small packages from private persons to private per-<br>sons, provided that the value of the products does not exceed 365<br>units of account;</p>
<p>(b) products forming part of travellers’ personal luggage, provided that<br>the value of the products does not exceed 1,025 units of account.</p>
<p>These provisions shall be applied only when such goods are not imported by<br>way of trade and have been declared as meeting the conditions required for<br>the application of the Agreement, and where there is no doubt as to the vera-<br>city of such declaration.</p>
<p>Importations which are occasional and consist solely of goods for the per-<br>sonal use of the recipients of travellers of their families shall not be conside-<br>red as importations by way of trade if it is evident from the nature and quan-<br>tity of the goods that no commercial purpose is in view.</p>
<p>3. Amounts in the national currency of the exporting Party to the Agree-<br>ment equivalent to the amounts expressed in units of account shall be fixed<br>by the exporting State and communicated to the other Party to the Agree-<br>ment. When the amounts are higher than the corresponding amounts fixed<br>by the importing State, the importing State shall accept them if the goods are<br>invoiced in the currency of the exporting State.</p>
<p>If the goods are invoiced in the currency of the other Party to the Agree-<br>ment, of Estonia or of Lithuania the importing State shall recognize the<br>amount notified by the State concerned.</p>
<p>32</p>
<p>4. The equivalent of a unit of account in the currencies of Latvia, Sweden,<br>Estonia or Lithuania shall be the amounts specified in Annex VI to this Pro-<br>tocol.</p>
<p>5. The amounts expressed in units of account should be reviewed whenever<br>necessary but anyway at least every second year.</p>
<p>6. Accessories, spare parts and tools dispatched with a piece of equipment,<br>machine, apparatus or vehicle which are part of the normal equipment and<br>included in the price thereof or are not separately invoiced are regarded as<br>one with the piece of equipment, machine, apparatus or vehicle in question.</p>
<p>7. Sets, within the meaning of General Rule 3 of the Harmonized System,<br>shall be regarded as originating when all component artides are originating<br>products. Nevertheless, when a set is composed of originating and non-origi-<br>nating artides, the set as a whole shall be regarded as originating provided<br>that the value of the non-originating artides does not exceed 15 per cent of<br>the ex-works price of the set.</p>
<p>Article 9</p>
<p>1. An EUR.l certificate shall be issued by the customs authorities of the<br>exporting State when the goods to which it relätes are exported. It shall be<br>made available to the exporter as soon as actual exportation has been effec-<br>ted or ensured.</p>
<p>2. The EUR. 1 certificate shall be issued by the customs authorities of Latvia<br>or Sweden if the goods to be exported can be considered as products origina-<br>ting in that State within the meaning of Article 1.</p>
<p>3. The customs authorities in Latvia or in Sweden may, provided that the<br>goods to be covered by the EUR.l certificates are in its territory, issue<br>EUR.l certificate under the conditions laid down in this Protocol if the<br>goods to be exported can be considered as products originating in Latvia or<br>in Sweden or in Estonia or in Lithuania within the meaning of Article 2.</p>
<p>In such cases, the issue of the EUR.l certificate is subject to the presenta-<br>tion of the evidence of origin issued or made out previously.</p>
<p>4. An EUR.l certificate may be issued only where it can serve as the docu-<br>mentary evidence required for the purpose of implementing the preferential<br>treatment provided for in this Agreement or the Agreements referred to in<br>sub-paragraph (b) (iii) of paragraph 1 of Article 1.</p>
<p>The date of issue of the EUR.l certificate must be indicated in the box on<br>the EUR.l certificate reserved for the customs authorities.</p>
<p>5. In exceptional circumstances an EUR.l certificate may also be issued af-<br>ter exportation of the goods to which it relätes if it was not issued at the time<br>of exportation because of errors, involuntary omissions of special circums-<br>tances.</p>
<p>The customs authorities may issue an EUR.l certificate retrospectively<br>only after verifying that the particulars supplied in the exporter’s application<br>agree with those on the corresponding document.</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>3 Riksdagen 1991/92. 1 saml. Nr 142</p>
<p>EUR.l certificates issued retrospectively must be endorsed with one of<br>the following phrases: “ISSUED RETROSPECTIVELY”, “UTFÄRDAT I<br>EFTERHAND”, “IZDOTS PÉC PREÖU EKSPORTA”, “TAGANTJÄ-<br>RELE VÄLJAANTUD”, “I§LEISTI ATGALINE DATA”.</p>
<p>6. In the event of the theft, loss or destruction of an EUR.l certificate, the<br>exporter may apply to the customs authorities which issued it for a duplicate<br>to be made out on the basis of the export documents in their possession. The<br>duplicate issued in this way must be endorsed with one of the following<br>words: “DUPLICATE”, “DUPLIKAT”, “DUBLIKÄTS”, “DUPLI-<br>KAAT”, “DUBLIKATAS”.</p>
<p>The duplicate, which must bear the date of issue of the original EUR.l<br>certificate, shall take effect as from that date.</p>
<p>7. The endorsements referred to in paragraphs 5 and 6 shall be inserted in<br>the “Remarks” box on the EUR.l certificate.</p>
<p>8. It shall always be possible to replace one or more EUR.l certificates by<br>one or more EUR.l certificates, provided that this is done at the customs<br>office where the goods are located.</p>
<p>9. For the purpose of verifying whether the conditions stated in paragraphs<br>2 and 3 have been met, the customs authorities shall have the right to call for<br>any documentaiy evidence or to carry out any check which they consider<br>approporiate.</p>
<p>10. The provisions of paragraphs 2 to 9 above shall apply, mutatis mutandis,<br>to the evidence of origin made out by approved exporters under the condi-<br>tions set out in Article 13.</p>
<p>Article 10</p>
<p>1. An EUR.l certificate shall be issued only on application having been<br>made in writing by the exporter or, under the exporter’s responsibility, by<br>his authorized representative, on the form of which a specimen is given in<br>Annex III to this Protocol, which shall be completed in accordance with this<br>Protocol.</p>
<p>2. It shall be the responsibility of the customs authorities of the exporting<br>State to ensure that the form referred to in paragraph 1 is properly comple-<br>ted. In particular, they shall check whether the box reserved for the descrip-<br>tion of the goods has been completed in such a manner as to exclude any<br>possibility of fraudulent additions. To this end, the description of the goods<br>must be given without leaving any blank lines. Where the box is not comple-<br>tely filled, a horizontal line must be drawn below the last line of the descrip-<br>tion, the empty space being crossed through.</p>
<p>3. Since the EUR.l certificate constitutes the documentary evidence for the<br>application of the preferential tariff and quota arrangements laid down in<br>the Agreement, it shall be the responsibility of the customs authorities of the<br>exporting country to take any steps necessary to verify the origin of the goods<br>and to check the other statements on the certificate.</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>34</p>
<p>4. When an EUR.l certificate is issued within the meaning of paragraph 5 Prop. 1991/92:142<br>of Article 9 after the goods to which it relätes have actually been exported, Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)<br>the exporter must in the application referred to in paragraph 1:</p>
<p>- indicate the place and date of exportation of the goods to which the</p>
<p>EUR.l certificate relätes,</p>
<p>- certify that no EUR.l certificates was issued at the time of exportation<br>of the goods in question, and State the reasons.</p>
<p>5. Application for EUR.l certificates and the evidence or origin referred to<br>in the second sub-paragraph of paragraph 3 of Article 9, upon presentation<br>of which new EUR.l certificates are issued, must be preserved for at least<br>two years by the customs authorities of the exporting country.</p>
<p>Article 11</p>
<p>1. EUR.l certificates shall be made out on the form of which a specimen of<br>which is given in Annex III to this Protocol. This form shall be printed in one<br>or more of the official languages of the States Parties to this Agreement or<br>in English. EUR.l certificates shall be made out in one of those languages<br>and in accordance with the provisions of the domestic law of the exporting<br>State; if they are handwritten, they shall be completed in ink in Capital let-<br>ters.</p>
<p>2. The EUR.l certificate shall be 210 x 297 millimetres. A tolerance of up<br>to plus 8 millimetres or minus 5 millimetres in the length may be allowed.<br>The paper used must be white-sized writing paper not containing mechanical<br>pulp and weighing not less than 25 grammes per square metre. It shall have<br>a printed green guilloche pattern background making any falsification by<br>mechanical or Chemical means apparent to the eye.</p>
<p>3. The States Parties to this Agreement may reserve the right to print the<br>EUR.l certificates themselves or may have them printed by printers appro-<br>ved by them. In the latter case, each EUR.l certificate must include a refe-<br>rence of such approval. Each EUR.l certificatemust bear the name and add-<br>ress of the printer or a mark by which the printer can be identified. It shall<br>also bear a serial number, whether or not printed, by which it can be identi-<br>fied.</p>
<p>Article 12</p>
<p>1. An EUR.l certificate must be submitted, within four months of the date<br>of issue by the customs authorities of the exporting State, to the customs aut-<br>horities of the importing State where the goods are entered, in accordance<br>with the procedures laid down by that State. The said authorities may require<br>a translation of a certificate. They may also require the import declaration<br>to be accompanied by a statement from the importer to the effect that the<br>goods meet the conditions required for the implementation of the Agree-<br>ment.</p>
<p>2. Without prejudice to paragraph 5 of Article 5, where, at the request of<br></p>
<p>35</p>
<p>the person declaring the goods at customs, a dismantled or non-assembled Prop. 1991/92:142<br>article falling within Chapter 84 or 85 of the Harmonized System is imported Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)<br>by instalments under the conditions laid down by the competent authorities,<br>it shall be considered to be a single article and an EUR.l certificate may be<br>submitted for the whole article upon importation of the first instalment.</p>
<p>3. An EUR.l certificate which is submitted to the customs authorities of the<br>importing State after the final date for presentation specified in paragraph 1<br>may be accepted for the purpose of applying preferential treatment, where<br>the failure to submit the certificate by the final date is due to force majeur<br>or exceptional circumstances.</p>
<p>In other cases of belated presentation, the customs authorities of the im-<br>porting State may accept the EUR.l certificates where the goods have been<br>submitted to them before the said final date.</p>
<p>4. The discovery of slight discrepancies between the statements made in the<br>EUR.l certificate and those made in the documents submitted to the Cus-<br>toms office for the purpose of carrying out the formalities for importing the<br>goods shall not ipso facto render the certificate null and void, provided it is<br>duly established that the certificate corresponds to the goods.</p>
<p>5. EUR.l certificates shall be preserved by the customs authorities of the<br>importing State in accordance with the rules in force in that State.</p>
<p>6. Proof that the conditions set out in Article 7 have been met shall be provi-<br>ded by submission to the customs authorities of the importing State of either:</p>
<p>(a) a single supporting transport document, made out in the exporting<br>State, under the cover of which the transit country has been crossed;</p>
<p>or</p>
<p>(b) a certificate issued by the customs authorities of the transit country</p>
<p>containing:</p>
<p>- an exact description of the goods,</p>
<p>- the date of unloading and reloading of the goods and, where appli-<br>cable, the names of the ships,</p>
<p>- certified proof of the conditions under which the goods have<br>stayed in the transit country;</p>
<p>(c) or, failing these, any substantiating documents.</p>
<p>Article 13</p>
<p>1. Notwithstanding paragraphs 1 to 7 of Article 9 and paragraphs 1, 4 and 5<br>of Article 10, a simplified procedure for the issue of the documentation rela-<br>ting to the evidence of origin shall be applicable under the terms of the provi-<br>sions set out below.</p>
<p>2. The customs authorities in the exporting State may authorize any expor-<br>ter, hereinafter referred to as “approved exporter”, who makes frequent<br>shipments for which EUR.l certificates may be issued, and who offers to the<br>satisfaction of the customs authorities all quarantees necessary to verify the<br>originating status of the goods, not to submit to the customs office in the<br></p>
<p>36</p>
<p>exporting State at the time of export either the goods or the application for Prop. 1991/92:142<br>an EUR.l certificate relating to those goods, for the purpose of obtaining an Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)<br>EUR.l certificate under the conditions laid down in paragraphs 1 to 4 of Ar-<br>ticle 9.</p>
<p>3. In addition, the customs authorities may authorize an approved exporter<br>to draw up EUR.l certificates, valid for a maximum period of one year from<br>the date of issue, hereinafter referred to as “LT certificates”. The authoriza-<br>tion shall be granted only where the originating status of the goods to be<br>exported is expected to remain unchanged for the period of validity of the<br>LT certificate. If any goods are no longer covered by the LT certificate, the<br>approved exporter shall immediately inform the customs authorities who<br>gave the authorization.</p>
<p>Where the simplified procedure applies, the customs authorities of the ex-<br>porting State may prescribe the use of EUR.l certificates bearing a distinc-<br>tive sign by which they may be identified.</p>
<p>4. The authorization referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3 shall stipulate, at the<br>choice of customs authorities, that Box 11, “Customs endorsement”, of the<br>EUR.l certificate must:</p>
<p>(a) either be endorsed beforehand with the stamp of the competent<br>customs office of the exporting State and the handwritten or non-<br>handwritten signature of an official of that office; or</p>
<p>(b) be endorsed by the approved exporter with a special stamp which<br>has been approved by the customs authorities of the exporting State<br>and corresponds to the specimen given in Annex V to this Protocol;<br>this stamp may be preprinted on the form.</p>
<p>Box 11, “Customs endorsement”, of the EUR.l certificate shall be comple-</p>
<p>ted if necessary by the approved exporter.</p>
<p>5. In the cases referred to in paragraph 4 (a), one of the following phrases<br>shall be entered in box 7, “Remarks”, of the EUR.l certificate: “Simplified<br>procedure”, “Förenklad procedur”, “Vienkärsotä procedura”, “Lihtsusta-<br>tud protseduur”, “Supaprastinta procedura”. The approved exporter shall if<br>necessary indicate in Box 13, “Request for verification”, the name and add-<br>ress of the customs authority competent to verify the EUR. 1 certificate.</p>
<p>6. In the case referred to in paragraph 3, the approved exporter shall also<br>enter in box 7 of the EUR.l certificate one of the following phrases:</p>
<p>“LT certificate valid until ...”,</p>
<p>“LT-certifikat giltigt till ...”,</p>
<p>“LT sertifikäts ir spékä lidz ...”,</p>
<p>“Pikaajaline sertifikaat kehtib kuni ...”,</p>
<p>“LT-sertificatas galioja iki</p>
<p>(date indicated in Arabic numerals),</p>
<p>and a reference to the authorization under which the relevant LT certificate<br>has been issued.</p>
<p>The approved exporter shall not be required to refer in Box 8 and Box 9<br></p>
<p>of the LT certificate to the marks and numbers and number and kind of pack-<br>ages and the gross weight (kg) or other measure (litres, m<sup>3</sup>, etc.). Box 8<br>must, however, contain a description and designation of the goods which is<br>sufficiently precise to allow for their identification.</p>
<p>7. Notwithstanding paragraphs 1 to 3 of Article 12, the LT certificate must<br>be submitted to the customs office of import at or before the first importation<br>of any goods to which it relätes. When the importer carries out the customs<br>clearance at several customs offices in the State of importation, the customs<br>authorities may request him to produce a copy of the LT certificate to all of<br>those offices.</p>
<p>8. Where an LT certificate has been submitted to the customs authorities,<br>the evidence of the originating status of the imported goods shall, during the<br>validity of the LT certificate, be given by invoices which satisfy the following<br>conditions:</p>
<p>(a) when an invoice includes both goods originating in Latvia, Sweden,<br>Estonia or Lithuania and non-originating goods, the exporter shall<br>distinguish clearly between these two categories;</p>
<p>(b) the exporter shall State on each invoice the number of the LT certifi-<br>cate which covers the goods and the date of expiry of the certificate<br>and the name(s) of the country or countries in which the goods ori-<br>ginate.</p>
<p>The statement on the invoice made by the exporter of the num-<br>ber of the LT certificate with the indication of the country of origin<br>shall constitute a declaration that the goods fulfil the conditions laid<br>down in this Protocol for the acquisition of preferential origin status<br>in trade between the States Parties to this Agreement.</p>
<p>The customs authorities of the exporting State may require that<br>the entries, which, under the above provisions, must appear on the<br>invoice, be supported by the manuscript signature followed by the<br>name of the signatory in clear script;</p>
<p>(c) the description and the designation of the goods on the invoice shall<br>be in sufficient detail to show clearly that the goods are also listed<br>on the LT certificate to which the invoice refers;</p>
<p>(d) the invoices can be made out only for the goods exported during<br>the period of validity of the relevant LT certificate. They may, ho-<br>wever, be produced at the import customs office within four months<br>of the date of their being made out by the exporter.</p>
<p>9. In the framework of the simplified procedures, invoices which satisfy the<br>conditions of this Article may be made out and/or transmitted using telecom-<br>munications or electronic data processing methods. Such invoices shall be<br>accepted by the customs of the importing State as evidence of the originating<br>status of the goods imported in accordance with the procedures laid down by<br>the customs authorities there.</p>
<p>10. Should the customs authorities of the exporting State identify that a cer-<br>tificate and/or invoice issued under the provisions of this Article is invalid<br>in relation to any goods supplied, they shall immediately notify the customs<br>authorities of the importing State of the facts.</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>38</p>
<p>11. The customs authorities may authorize an approved exporter to make<br>out invoices bearing the declaration given in Annex IV to this Protocol in<br>place of EUR.l certificates.</p>
<p>The declaration made by the approved exporter on the invoice shall be<br>made out in one of the official languages of the Parties to this Agreement or<br>in English. It shall be signed in manuscript and must either:</p>
<p>(a) have a reference to the approved exporter’s authorization number,<br>or</p>
<p>(b) be endorsed by the approved exporter with the special stamp refer-<br>red to in paragraph 4 (b) which has been approved by the customs<br>authorities of the exporting State. This stamp may be preprinted on<br>the invoice.</p>
<p>12. However, the customs authorities in the exporting State may authorize<br>an approved exporter not to sign the statement in paragraph 8 (b) or the<br>declaration referred to in paragraph 11 given on the invoice, when such in-<br>voices are made out and/or transmitted using telecommunication or electro-<br>nic data processing methods.</p>
<p>The said customs authorities shall lay down conditions for the implemen-<br>tation of this paragraph, including, if they so require, a written undertaking<br>from the approved exporter, that he accepts full responsibility for such state-<br>ment and declaration as if they had in fact been signed in manuscript by him.</p>
<p>13. In the authorization referred to in paragraphs 2, 3 and 11 the customs<br>authorities shall specify in particular:</p>
<p>(a) the conditions under which the application for EUR.l certificates<br>or for LT certificates are made or under which the declaration con-<br>cerning the origin of goods is made on the invoice;</p>
<p>(b) the conditions under which these applications, as well as a copy of<br>the invoices referring to an LT certificate and of the invoices bea-<br>ring the exporter’s declaration, are kept for at least two years. In<br>the case of LT certificates or invoices referring to an LT certificate,<br>this period shall begin from the date of expiry of validity of the LT<br>certificate. These provisions shall also apply to the EUR. 1 certifi-<br>cates or LT certificates and the invoices referring to an LT certifi-<br>cate, as well as to invoices bearing the exporter’s declaration, ha-<br>ving served as the basis for the issue of other evidence of origin,<br>used under the conditions laid down in the second sub-paragraph<br>of paragraph 3 of Article 9.</p>
<p>14. The customs authorities in the exporting State may declare certain cate-<br>gories of goods ineligible for the special treatment provided for in para-<br>graphs 2, 3 and 11.</p>
<p>15. The customs authorities shall refuse the authorization referred to in pa-<br>ragraphs 2, 3 and 11 to exporters who do not offer all the guarantees which<br>they consider necessary.</p>
<p>The customs authorities may withdraw the authorizations at any time.<br>They must do so where the conditions of approval are no longer satisfied or<br>the approved exporter no longer offers those guarantees.</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>39</p>
<p>16. The approved exporter may be required to inform the customs authori-<br>ties, in accordance with the rules which they lay down, of goods to be dispatc-<br>hed by him, so that the competent customs office may make any verification<br>it thinks necessary before the dispatch of the goods.</p>
<p>17. The provisions of this Article shall not prejudice application of the rules<br>of the States Parties to this Agreement on customs formalities and the use of<br>customs documents.</p>
<p>Article 14</p>
<p>The declaration referred to in paragraph 1 (c) of Article 8 shall be made out<br>by the exporter in the form given in Annex IV to this Protocol in one of the<br>official languages of the States Parties to this Agreement or in English. It<br>shall be typed or stamped and signed by hand. The exporter must keep a<br>copy of the invoice bearing the said declaration for at least two years.</p>
<p>Article 15</p>
<p>1. The exporter or his representative shall submit with his request for an<br>EUR.l certificate any appropriate supporting document proving that the<br>goods to be exported qualify for the issue of an EUR.l certificate.</p>
<p>He shall undertake to submit at the request of the appropriate authorities,<br>any supplementary evidence they may require for the purpose of establishing<br>the correctness of the originating status of the goods eligible for preferential<br>treatment and shall undertake to agree to any inspection of his accounts and<br>to any check on the processes of the obtaining of the above goods, carried<br>out by the said authorities.</p>
<p>2. Exporters must keep for at least two years the supporting documents re-<br>ferred to in paragraph 1.</p>
<p>3. The provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2 shall apply mutatis mutandis in the<br>case of the use of the procedures laid down in paragraphs 2 and 3 of Article<br>13 and of the declarations referred to in paragraphs 1 (b) and 1 (c) of Article</p>
<p>8.</p>
<p>Article 16</p>
<p>1. Goods sent from Latvia or Sweden for exhibition in a country other than<br>Latvia, Sweden, Estonia or Lithuania and sold after the exhibition for im-<br>portation into Latvia or Sweden shall benefit on importation from the provi-<br>sions of this Agreement on condition that the goods meet the requirements<br>of this Protocol entitling them to be recognized as originating in Sweden or<br>Latvia and provided that it is shown to the satisfaction of the customs autho-<br>rities that:</p>
<p>(a) an exporter has consigned these goods from Latvia or from Sweden<br>to the country in which the exhibition is held and has exhibited<br>them there;</p>
<p>(b) the goods have been sold or otherwise disposed of by that exporter<br>to someone in Sweden or Latvia;</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>(c) the goods have been consigned during the exhibition or immedia-<br>tely thereafter to Sweden or Latvia in the State in which they were<br>sent for exhibition;</p>
<p>(d) the goods have not, since they were consigned for exhibition, been<br>used for any purpose other than demonstration at the exhibition.</p>
<p>2. An EUR.l certificate must be produced to the customs authorities in the<br>normal manner. The name and address of the exhibition must be indicated<br>thereon. Where necessary, additional documentary evidence of the nature<br>of the goods and the conditions under which they have been exhibited may<br>be required.</p>
<p>3. Paragraph 1 shall apply to any trade, industrial, agricultural or crafts exhi-<br>bition, fair or similar public show or display which is not organized for pri-<br>vate purposes in shops or business premises with a view to the sale of foreign<br>goods, and during which the goods remain under customs control.</p>
<p>Article 17</p>
<p>1. In order to ensure the proper application of this Title, Latvia and Sweden<br>shall assist each other through their respective customs administrations, in<br>checking the authenticity and accuracy of EUR.l certificates, including<br>those issued under paragraph 3 of Article 9 and the exporters’ declarations<br>made on invoices.</p>
<p>2. The Joint Committee shall be authorized to take any decisions necessary<br>for the methods of administrative cooperation to be applied in due time in<br>Latvia and Sweden.</p>
<p>3. The customs authorities of Latvia and Sweden shall provide each other<br>with specimen impressions of stamps used in their customs offices for the<br>issue of EUR.l certificates.</p>
<p>4. Penalties shall be imposed on any person who draws up, or causes to be<br>drawn up, a document which contains incorrect particulars for the purpose<br>of obtaining a preferential treatment for goods.</p>
<p>5. Latvia and Sweden shall take all necessary steps to ensure that goods tra-<br>ded under cover of an EUR.l certificate, which in the course of transport<br>use a free zone situated in their territory, are not substituted by other goods<br>and that they do not undergo handling other than normal operations desig-<br>ned to prevent their deterioration.</p>
<p>6. When products originating in Latvia and Sweden and imported into a free<br>zone under cover of an EUR.l certificate undergo treatment or processing,<br>the customs authorities concerned must issue a new EUR.l certificate at the<br>exporter’s request if the treatment or processing undergone is in conformity<br>with the provisions of this Protocol.</p>
<p>Article 18</p>
<p>1. Subsequent verifications of EUR.l certificates and of exporters’ declara-<br>tions made on invoices shall be carried out at random or whenever the cus-</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>toms authorities of the importing State have reasonable doubt as to the aut-<br>henticity of the document or the accuracy of the information regarding the<br>true origin of the goods in question.</p>
<p>2. For the purposes of implementing the provisions of paragraph 1, the cus-<br>toms authorities of the importing State shall return the EUR.l certificate<br>and the invoice, if it has been submitted, or the invoice referring to an LT<br>certificate, or the invoice bearing the exporter’s declaration or a copy of<br>those documents, to the customs authorities of the exporting State, giving<br>where appropriate, the reasons of substance or form for an inquiry.</p>
<p>The customs authorities shall forward, in support of the request for a pos-<br>teriori verification, any documents and information that have been obtained<br>suggesting that the particulars given on the EUR.l certificate or the invoice<br>are inaccurate.</p>
<p>If the customs authorities of the importing State decide to suspend the pro-<br>visions of the Agreement while awaiting the results of the verification, they<br>shall offer to release the goods to the importer subject to any precautionary<br>measures judged necessary.</p>
<p>3. The customs authorities of the importing State shall be informed of the<br>results of the verification as soon as possible. These results must be such as<br>to make it possible to determine whether the documents returned under pa-<br>ragraph 2 apply to the goods actually exported, and whether these goods can,<br>in fact, qualify for application of the preferential arrangements.</p>
<p>Where such disputes cannot be settled between the customs authorities of<br>the importing State and those of the exporting State or where they raise a<br>question as to the interpretation of this Protocol they shall be submitted to<br>the Sub-Committee on customs and origin matters referred to in Article 26.<br>The decisions shall be taken by the Joint Committee.</p>
<p>For the purpose of the subsequent verification of EUR.l certificates, the<br>customs authorities of the exporting country must keep the export docu-<br>ments, or copies of EUR.l certificates used in place thereof, for at least two<br>year.</p>
<p>Title III</p>
<p>Final provisions</p>
<p>Article 19</p>
<p>Latvia and Sweden shall each take the steps necessary to implement this Pro-<br>tocol.</p>
<p>Article 20</p>
<p>The Annexes to this Protocol shall form an integral part thereof.</p>
<p>Article 21</p>
<p>Goods which conform to the provisions of Title I and which on the date of<br>entry into force of the Agreement are either being transported or are being<br></p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>held in Latvia or Sweden in temporary storage, in bonded warehouses or in<br>free zones, may be accepted as originating products subject to the submis-<br>sion - within four months from that date - to the customs authorities of the<br>importing State of an evidence of origin, drawn up retrospectively, and of<br>any documents that provide supporting evidence of the conditions of trans-<br>port.</p>
<p>Article 22</p>
<p>Latvia and Sweden undertake to introduce measures necessary to ensure<br>that the EUR.l certificates which their customs authorities are authorized to<br>issue in pursuance of this Agreement are issued under the conditions laid<br>down by this Agreement. They also undertake to provide the administrative<br>co-operation necessary for this purpose, in particular to check on the itine-<br>rary of goods traded under this Agreement and the places in which they have<br>been held.</p>
<p>Article 23</p>
<p>1. Without prejudice to the provisions of Protocol A, products which are of<br>the kind to which the Agreement applies, and which are used in the manufac-<br>ture of products for which an EUR.l certificate, an LT certificate or the in-<br>voices referring to the LT certificate, or an invoice bearing the exporter’s<br>declaration are issued or completed, can only be the subject of drawback of<br>customs duty or benefit from an exemption of customs duty of whatever kind<br>when products originating in Latvia, Sweden, Estonia or Lithuania are con-<br>cerned.</p>
<p>2. In this Article, the term “customs duty” also means charges having an<br>effect equivalent to customs duty.</p>
<p>Article 24</p>
<p>(This Protocol does not contain an Article 24)</p>
<p>Article 25</p>
<p>1. Originating products within the meaning of this Protocol shall, on impor-<br>tation into Latvia benefit from the Agreement also upon submission of an<br>EUR.l certificate issued by a customs office in Estonia or Lithuania in which<br>the expression “Application Article 25” has been inserted and authenticated<br>by the stamp of the said office.</p>
<p>2. When products, previously imported into Latvia accompanied by evi-<br>dence of origin referred to in paragraph 1 of Article 8, issued or made out in<br>Sweden, are re-exported to Estonia or to Lithuania, Latvia shall undertake<br>to issue EUR.l certificates with the expression “Application Article 25”,<br>provided that the products are re-exported in the same State or have under-<br>gone no working or processing in Latvia going beyond that referred to in<br>paragraph 5 of Article 5.</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>
<p>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</p>
<p>43</p>
<p>Article 26</p>
<p>A Sub-Committee on customs and origin matters shall be set up under the<br>Joint Committee in accordance with paragraph 4 of Article 21 of the Agree-<br>ment charged with carrying out administrative cooperation with a view to<br>ensuring a practical, correct and uniform application of this Protocol as well<br>as a continuous information and consultation process between experts.</p>
<p>It shall be composed of experts from Latvia and Sweden responsible for<br>questions related to origin rules.</p>
<p>Article 27</p>
<p>For the purpose of implementing sub-paragraph (b) (ii) or (iii) of paragraph<br>1 of Article 1 any product originating in the territory of Latvia or Sweden<br>shall, on exportation to the territory of the other Party to this Agreement,<br>be treated as a non-originating product during the period or periods in which<br>the last-mentioned Party to this Agreement applies the rate of duty appli-<br>cable to third countries or any corresponding safeguard measure to such pro-<br>ducts in accordance with this Agreement.</p>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142</p>

<p>ANNEX I</p>
<p>EXPLANATORY NOTES</p>
<p>Note 1 - Article 1</p>
<p>The term &quot;State Party to this Agreement&quot; shall also<br>cover the territorial waters of this State.</p>
<p>Vessels operating on the high seas, including factory<br>ships, on which the fish caught is worked or processed<br>shall be considered as part of the territory of the State<br>Party to this Agreement to which they belong provided that<br>they satisfy the conditions set out in Explanatory Note 4.</p>
<p>Note 2 - Artides 1, 2 and 4</p>
<p>The conditions set out in Article 1 relative to the<br>acquisition of originating status must be fulfilled without<br>interruption in a State Party to this Agreement except as<br>provided for in Article 2.</p>
<p>If originating products exported from a State Party to<br>this Agreement to another country are returned, except so<br>far as provided for in Article 2, they must be considered<br>as non-originating unless it can be demonstrated to the<br>satisfaction of the customs authorities that:</p>
<p>the goods returned are the same goods as those<br>exported, and</p>
<p>they have not undergone any operations beyond<br>that necessary to preserve them in good condition<br>while in that country.</p>
<p>Note 3 - Artides 1 and 2</p>
<p>In order to determine whether goods are originating<br>products it shall not be necessary to establish whether the<br>power and fuel, plant and equipment, and machines and tools<br>used to obtain such goods originate in third countries or<br>not.</p>
<p>Note 4 - sub-paragraph (f) of Article 4</p>
<p>The term &quot;its vessels&quot; shall apply only to vessels:</p>
<p>(a) which are registered or recorded in a State Party<br>to this Agreement;</p>
<h2>45</h2>
<h2>Prop. 1991/92:142</h2>
<h2>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</h2>
<p>(b) &nbsp;which sail under the flag of a State Party to<br>this Agreement;</p>
<p>(c) &nbsp;which are at least 50 per cent owned by nationals<br>of a State Party to this Agreement or by a<br>company with its head office in such a State, of<br>which the manager or managers, chairman of the<br>board of directors or of the supervisory board,<br>and the majority of the members of such boards<br>are nationals of a State Party to this Agreement<br>and of which, in addition, in the case of<br>partnerships or limited companies, at least half<br>of the Capital belongs to such a State or to<br>public bodies or nationals of such a State;</p>
<p>(d) &nbsp;of which the captain and officers are all<br>nationals of a State Party to this Agreement;</p>
<p>(e) &nbsp;of which at least 75 per cent of the crew are<br>nationals of a State Party to this Agreement.</p>
<p>Note 5 - Artides 4 and 5</p>
<p>1. &nbsp;&nbsp;The unit of qualification for the application of the<br>origin rules shall be the particular product which is<br>considered as the basic unit when determining</p>
<p>classification using the Nomenclature of the Harmonized<br>System. In the case of 6ets of products which are<br>classified by virtue of General Rule 3, the unit of<br>qualification shall be determined in respect of each item<br>in the set; this also applies to the sets of heading Nos<br>6308,8206 and 9605.</p>
<p>Accordingly, it follows that:</p>
<p>when a product composed of a group or assembly of<br>artides is classified under the terms of the<br>Harmonized System within a single heading, the<br>whole constitutes the unit of qualification,</p>
<p>when a consignment consists of a number of<br>identical products classified within the same<br>heading of the harmonized system, each product<br>must be taken individually when applying the<br>origin rules.</p>
<p>2. &nbsp;&nbsp;Where, under General Rule 5 of the Harmonized System,<br>packing is included with the product for classification<br>purposes, it shall be included for purposes of determining<br>origin.</p>

<p>Note 6 - Paragraph 2 of Article 5</p>
<p>The Introductory Kotes to Annex II shall also apply<br>where appropriate to all products manufactured using non-<br>originating Materials even if they are not subject to a<br>specific condition contained in the list in Annex II but<br>are subject instead to the change of heading rule set out<br>in paragraph 2 of Article 5.</p>
<p>Note 7 - Article 6</p>
<p>&quot;Ex-works price&quot; shall Mean the price paid to the<br>Manufacturer in whose undertaking the last working or<br>processing is carried out, provided the price includes the<br>value of all the products used in Manufacture.</p>
<p>&quot;Customs value&quot; shall be understood as meaning the<br>customs value as determined in accordance with the<br>Agreement on implementation of Article VII of the General<br>Agreement on Tariffs and Trade done at Geneva on 12 April<br>1979.</p>
<p>Note 8 - Paragraph 1 of Article 8</p>

<p>In the case of products sent by post which, within the<br>Meaning of paragraph 2 of Article 8, are not considered as<br>importations by way of trade, the declaration of the<br>originating status can also be Made on the customs<br>declaration C2/CP3 or on a sheet of paper annexed to that<br>declaration.</p>
<p>Note 9 - Paragraph 1 of Article 17 and Article 22</p>

<p>&quot;Drawback of customs duty or exemption from customs<br>duty of whatever kind&quot; shall mean any arrangement for<br>refund or remission, partial or complete, of customs duties<br>applicable to products used in manufacture, provided that<br>the said provision concedes, expressly or in effect, this<br>repayment or non-charging or the non-imposition when goods<br>obtained from the said products are exported but not when<br>they are retained for home use.</p>
<p>&quot;Products used in manufacture&quot; shall mean any products<br>in respect of which a &quot;drawback of customs duty or<br>exemption from customs duty of whatever kind&quot; is requested<br>as a result of the export of originating products for which<br>an EUR.l certificate, an LT certificate or the invoices<br>referring to the LT certificate, or an invoice bearing the<br>exporter'6 declaration are issued or made out.</p>

<h2>Prop. 1991/92:142</h2>
<h2>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</h2>
<p>ANNEX II</p>
<p>List of working or processing required to be carried out on<br>non-originating materials in order that the product<br>manufactured can obtain originating status</p>
<p>INTRODUCTORY NOTES</p>
<p>General</p>
<p>Kote 1</p>
<p>1.1 &nbsp;The first two columns in the List describe the<br>products obtained. The first column gives the<br>heading number, or the Chapter number, used in<br>the Harmonized System and the second column gives<br>the description of goods used in that System for<br>that heading or Chapter. For each entry in the<br>first two columns a rule is specified in columns<br>3 and 4. Where, in some cases, the entry in the<br>first column is preceded by an &quot;ex&quot;, this<br>signifies that the rule in column 3 or column 4<br>only applies to the part of that heading or<br>Chapter as described in column 2.</p>
<p>1.2 &nbsp;Where several heading numbers are grouped<br>together in column 1 or a Chapter is given and<br>the description of product in column 2 is<br>therefore given in general terms, the adjacent<br>rule in column 3 or column 4 applies to all<br>products which, under the Harmonized System, are<br>classified within headings of the Chapter or<br>within any of the headings grouped together in<br>column 1.</p>
<p>1.3 &nbsp;Where there are different rules in the List<br>applying to different products within a heading,<br>each indent contains the description of that part<br>of the heading covered by the adjacent rule in<br>column 3 or column 4.</p>
<p>1.4 &nbsp;For the products of Chapters 84 and 91 inclusive,<br>if no origin rule is given in column 4, the rule<br>set out in column 3 has to be applied.</p>
<p>Note 2</p>
<p>2.1 The term &quot;manufacture&quot; covers any kind of working<br>or processing including &quot;assembly&quot; or specific<br>operations. However, see paragraph 5 of Note 3.<br>below.</p>
<p>4 Riksdagen 199H92. 1 saml. Nr 142</p>
<h2>Prop. 1991/92:142<br>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</h2>
<p>2.2 &nbsp;The tern &quot;material&quot; covere any &quot;ingredient&quot;, &quot;raw<br>material&quot;, &quot;component&quot; or &quot;part&quot;, etc., used in<br>the manufacture of the product.</p>
<p>2.3 &nbsp;The term &quot;product&quot; refers to the product being<br>manufactured, even if it is intended for later<br>use in another manufacturing operation.</p>
<p>Note 3</p>
<p>3.1 &nbsp;In the case of any heading not in the List or any<br>part of a heading that is not in the List, the<br>&quot;change of heading&quot; rule set out in paragraph 2<br>of Article 5 applies. If a &quot;change of heading&quot;<br>condition applies to any entry in the List, then<br>it is contained in the rule in column 3.</p>
<p>3.2 &nbsp;The working or processing required by a rule in<br>column 3 or column 4 has to be carried out only<br>in relation to the non-originating materials<br>U6ed. The restrictions contained in a rule in<br>column 3 or column 4 likewise apply only to the<br>non-originating materials used.</p>
<p>3.3 &nbsp;Where a rule States that &quot;materials of any<br>heading&quot; may be used, materials of the same<br>heading as the product may also be used, subject,<br>however, to any specific limitations which may<br>also be contained in the rule. However, the<br>expression &quot;manufacture from materials of any<br>heading including other materials of heading<br>No...&quot; means that only materials classified<br>within the same heading as the product of a<br>different description than that of the product as<br>given in column 2 of the List may be used.</p>
<p>3.4 &nbsp;If a product, made from non-originating materials<br>which has acquired originating status during<br>manufacture by virtue of the change of heading<br>rule or its own List rule, is used as a material<br>in the process of manufacture of another product,<br>then the rule applicable to the product in which<br>it is incorporated does not apply to it.</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<p>an engine of heading No. 8407, for which the<br>rule States that the value of the non-<br>originating materials which may be<br>incorporated may not exceed 40 * of the ex-<br>works price, is made from &quot;other alloy Steel<br>roughly shaped by forging&quot; of heading No.<br>7224.</p>
<h2>50</h2>
<h2>Prop. 1991/92:142</h2>
<h2>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</h2>
<p>If this forging has been forged in the<br>country concerned from a non-originating<br>ingot then the forging has already acguired<br>origin by virtue of the rule for heading No.<br>ex 7224 in the List. It can then count as<br>originating in the value calculation for the<br>engine regardless of whether it was produced<br>in the same factory or another. The value<br>of the non-originating ingot is thus not<br>taken into account when adding up the value<br>of the non-originating materials used.</p>
<p>3.5 Even if the change of heading rule or the rule<br>contained in the List are satisfied, a product<br>does not have origin if the processing carried<br>out, taken as a whole, is insufficient in the<br>sense of paragraph 5 of Article 5.</p>
<p>Note 4</p>
<p>4.1 &nbsp;The rule in the List represents the minimum<br>amount of working or processing required and the<br>carrying out or more working or processing also<br>confers originating status; conversely, the<br>carrying out of less working or processing cannot<br>confer origin. Thus if a rule says that non-<br>originating material at a certain level of<br>manufacture may be used, the use of such material<br>at an earlier stage of manufacture is allowed and<br>the use of such material at later stage is not.</p>
<p>4.2 &nbsp;When a rule in the List specifies that a product<br>may be manufactured from more than one material,<br>this means that any one or more of the materials<br>may be used. It does not require that all be<br>used.</p>
<p>For »rample:</p>
<p>The rule for fabrics says that natural<br>fibres may be used and that Chemical<br>materials, among other materials, may also<br>be used. This does not mean that both have<br>to be used, one can use one or the other or<br>both.</p>
<p>If, however, a restriction applies to one<br>material and other restrictions apply to other<br>materials in the same rule, then the restrictions<br>only apply to the materials actually used.</p>
<p>- For example:</p>
<p>The rule for sewing machines specifies that<br>the thread tension mechanism used has to<br>originate and that the zigzag mechanism used</p>
<h2>51</h2>
<h2>Prop. 1991/92:142</h2>
<h2>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</h2>
<p>also has to originate; these two<br>restrictions only apply if the mechanisms<br>concerned are actually incorporated into the<br>aewing machine.</p>
<p>4.3 &nbsp;When a rule in the List specifies that a product<br>must be manufactured from a particular material,<br>the condition obviously does not prevent the use<br>of other materials which, because of their<br>inherent nature, cannot satisfy the rule.</p>
<p>- For axample:</p>
<p>The rule for heading No. 1904 which<br>specifically excludes the use of cereal6 or<br>their derivatives does not prevent the use<br>of mineral salts, Chemicals and other<br>additives which are not produced from<br>cereals.</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<p>In the case of an article made from non-<br>woven materials, if the use of only non-<br>originating yarn is allowed for this class<br>of article, it is not possible to start from<br>non-woven cloth - even if non-wovens cannot<br>normally be made from yarn. In such cases,<br>the starting material would normally be at<br>the stage before yarn - that i6 the fibre<br>stage.</p>
<p>See also paragraph 3 of Note 7 in relation to<br>textiles.</p>
<p>4.4 &nbsp;If in a rule in the List two or more percentages<br>are given for the maximum value of non-<br>originating materials that can be used, then<br>these percentages may not be added together. The<br>maximum value of all the non-originating<br>materials used may never exceed the highest of<br>the percentages given. Furthermore the<br>individual percentages must not be exceeded in<br>relation to the particular materials they apply<br>to.</p>
<p>Textiles</p>
<p>Note 5</p>
<p>5.1 The term &quot;natural fibres&quot; is used in the List to<br>refer to fibres other than artificial or<br>synthetic fibres and is restricted to the stages<br>before spinning takes place, including waste and<br>unless otherwise specified, the term &quot;natural</p>
<h2>52</h2>
<h2>Prop. 1991/92:142<br>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</h2>
<p>fibres&quot; includes fibres that have been carded,<br>conbed or otherwise processed but not spun.</p>
<p>5.2 &nbsp;The tern &quot;natural fibres&quot; includes horsehair of<br>heading No. 0503, silk of headings Nos. 5002 and<br>5003 as vell as the wool fibres, fine or coarse<br>animal hair of headings Nos. 5101 to 5105, the<br>cotton fibres of headings Nos. 5201 to 5203 and<br>the other vegetable fibres of headings Nos. 5301<br>to 5305.</p>
<p>5.3 &nbsp;The teras &quot;textile pulp&quot;, &quot;chenical naterials&quot;<br>and &quot;paper-naking naterials&quot; are used in the List<br>to describe the naterials not classified within<br>Chapters 50 to 63 which can be used to<br>nanufacture artificial, synthetic or paper fibres<br>or yarns.</p>
<p>5.4 &nbsp;The tern &quot;nan-nade staple fibres&quot; is used in the<br>List to refer to synthetic or artificial filanent<br>tow, staple fibres or waste, of headings Nos.<br>5501 to 5507.</p>
<p>Note 6</p>
<p>6.1 &nbsp;In the case of the products classified within<br>those headings in the List to which reference is<br>nade to this Introductory Note, the conditions<br>set out in colunn 3 of the List shall not be<br>applied to any basic textile naterials used in<br>their nanufacture which, taken together,<br>represent 10 % or less of the total weight of all<br>the basic textile naterials used (but see also<br>paragraphs 3 and 4 of Note 6 below).</p>
<p>6.2 &nbsp;However, this tolerance nay only be applied to<br>nixed products which have been nade fron two or<br>nore basic textile naterials, irrespective of<br>their share of the product.</p>
<p>The following are the basic textile naterials:<br>silk,<br>wool,<br>coarse aninal hair,</p>
<p>- &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fine aninal hair,<br>horsehair,</p>
<p>- &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cotton,</p>
<p>paper-naking naterials and paper,<br>flax,</p>
<p>- &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;true henp,</p>
<p>jute and other textile bast fibres,<br>■isal and other textile fibres of the genus<br>Agava,</p>
<h2>53</h2>
<p>Prop. 1991/92:142<br>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)<br>coconut, abaca, ramie and other vegetable<br>textile fibres,<br>synthetic man-made filaments,<br>artificial man-made filaments,<br>synthetic man-made staple fibres,<br>artificial man-made staple fibres.</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<p>A yarn of heading No. 5205 sade from cotton<br>fibres and synthetic staple fibres is a<br>mixed yarn. Therefore, non-originating<br>materials that do not satisfy the origin<br>rules may be used up to a weight of 10 * of<br>the yarn.</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<p>A woollen fabric of heading No. 5112 made<br>from woollen yarn and synthetic yarn of<br>staple fibres is a mixed fabric. Therefore,<br>either non-originating synthetic yarn or<br>woollen yarn or a combination thereof that<br>does not satisfy the origin rules may be<br>used up to a weight of 10 % of the fabric</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<p>Tufted textile of heading No. 5802 made from<br>cotton yarn and cotton fabric is only a<br>mixed product if the cotton fabric i6 itself<br>a mixed fabric being made from two or more<br>different basic textile materials or if the<br>cotton yarns used are themselves mixtures.</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<p>If the tufted textile concerned had been<br>made from cotton yarn and synthetic fabric,<br>then, obviously, two separate basic textile<br>materials would have been used.</p>
<p>For example:</p>
<p>A carpet with tufts made both from<br>artificial yarns and tufts made from cotton<br>yarns and with a jute backing is a mixed<br>product because three basic textile<br>materials are used. Thus, any non-<br>originating materials that are used at a<br>later stage of manufacture than the rule<br>allows, may be used, provided their total<br>weight taken together does not exceed 10 %<br>of the weight of the textile materials in<br>the carpet. Thus, the jute backing, the<br>artificial yarns and/or the cotton yarns<br>could be imported at that stage of<br>manufacture, provided the weight conditions<br>are met.</p>
<h2>54</h2>
<h2>Prop. 1991/92:142</h2>
<h2>Bilaga 1 (Prot. A)</h2>
<p>6.3 &nbsp;In the caee of products incorporating &quot;yarn made<br>of polyurethane segmented with flexible segments<br>of polyether whether or not gimped&quot; this<br>tolerance is 20 % in respect of this yarn.</p>
<p>6.4 &nbsp;In the case of products incorporating strip<br>con6isting of a core of aluminium foil or of a<br>core of plastic film whether or not coated with<br>aluminium powder, of a width not exceeding 5 mm.,<br>sandwiched by means of an adhesive between two<br>films of plastic film, this tolerance is 30 % in<br>respect of this strip.</p>
<p>Note 7</p>
<p>7.1 &nbsp;In the case of those textile products, which are<br>marked in the List by a footnote referring to<br>this Introductory Note, textile materials, with<br>the exception of linings and interlinings, which<br>do not sati6fy the rule set out in the List in<br>column 3 for the made-up product concerned may be<br>used provided that they are classified in a<br>heading other than that of the product and that<br>their value does not exceed 8 % of the ex-works<br>price of the product.</p>
<p>7.2 &nbsp;Any non-textile trimmings and accessories or<br>other materials used which contain textiles do<br>not have to satisfy the conditions set out in<br>column 3 even though they fall outside the 6cope<br>of paragraph 3 of Note 4.</p>
<p>7.3 &nbsp;In accordance with paragraph 3 of Note 4, any<br>non-originating non-textile trimmings and<br>accessories or other product, which do not<br>contain any textiles, may, anyway, be used freely<br>where they cannot be made from the materials<br>listed in column 3.</p>
<p>For »xaaple:</p>
<p>If a rule in the List says that for a<br>particular textile item, such as a blouse,<br>yarn must be used, this does not prevent the<br>use of metal items, such as buttons, because<br>they cannot be made from textile materials.</p>
<p>7.4 Where a percentage rule applies, the value of<br>trimmings and accessories must be taken into<br>account when calculating the value of the non-<br>originating materials incorporated.</p>
